Stockport v. Little Lever.
This match was played at Little Lever in splendid weather and before a large attendance of spectators. A start was not made till quite three o'clock owing to the Stockport men being delayed on the road. The match was set apart for the benefit of Penny, one of the Little Lever professionals, and one who has done splendid service with the ball, this being his first year with the club. Little Lever deplored the services of Fred Torkington and one or two others, while Little Lever had their strongest team in the field this season. Little Lever won the toss, and electing to bat sent in Towler and Tyldesley to face the bowling of Brown and Tyler. Tyldesley had a splendid reception on coming out—a fact due, no doubt, to that player being admitted to the Lancashire County, and it will be recalled in this connection that on his second appearance for his county he scored no fewer than 158 not out against Warwickshire. Brown gave way to Towler, landing him first ball, and the next ball bowled him leg stump. A. Smith came next, but after scoring six in a wretched fashion Brown also took this wicket. Tyldesley, the Lancashire County wicket-keeper, joined Tyldesley, but immediately after Tyldesley was splendidly taken by Bates at slip, on the leg side, and three good wickets were down for seven. Pool came next, and soon began to force matters, hitting Brown out of the ground for 6; may b the wicket, however, is a very small one indeed, it being no trouble to get a ball out. Smith seemed content with singles. The score went steadily on, when Brown's bowling was tried at 30. Harry May displacing Tyler; the change almost worked immediately, May bowling Tyldesley well hit 20. Pool came on next, and got May away to leg nicely for three, but at the other end Brown bowled him with a grand ball, and the score was severed at 45 runs. Simm joined Smith; the latter with his score at 16 was missed by Bates at long off. Simm was the next victim, Brown repeating his wicket 51—6—0. Knutton followed, and hit up 11 in four hits, but was then beautifully taken by Harold Hartley off Brown. 62—7. Then Northrop came next, and here a little stand was made, Northrop getting May away for three while Smith hit the same bowler for a like number. The score had reached 81 when Brown disturbed Smith's wicket for a lucky innings of 32. A strange coincidence took place during Smith's innings, and one which certainly did not reflect much credit on the Little Lever umpire. W. Hartley, who had displaced May, was pulling one to leg in his second over, Smith hit the ball out to Bates at square leg and was caught, the umpire, in the meantime, saying "over," and when Bates had caught Smith the umpire gave it a "no ball," and thus Smith was allowed to proceed with his innings. The sad soon came, the innings closing for 31. Penny Brown deserves great credit for his splendid bowling, taking no fewer than right wickets for 37 runs, hitting the stumps six times, while the other two were caught. Stockport opened their venture in a dreadful bad light, J. Bates and W. Hartley being the first batsmen to face Knutton and Penny. Bates after scoring a single was caught at the wicket. A. Torkington joined his captain, but after scoring two shares the rest of Bates, Knutton came next, and hitting one out to Tyldesley was splendidly caught and three wickets were down for 11 runs. Rain then commenced to fall, and put a stop to all further play, and what would have been an interesting finish never came off. The Stockport men fielded quite up to form. On Saturday next Wor. neth are down at Cale Green, and this match is set apart for the benefit of both Brown and Jack Dixon. As this is one of the best fixtures on the card and a fixture which takes well with the Stockport people, the two "pros" will materially benefit by it. Given a fine day, a grand game is expected. So roll up and assist your old friends. Below are appended the score and analysis:—

ST. JOSEPH'S (REDDISH) v. ST. THOMAS' (HYDE).—St. Joseph's met St. Thomas' at Hyde on Saturday, the match being a compliment one. The home team went to the wicket first, and were disposed of for 27 runs. St. Joseph's scored 29 for four wickets, thus winning by two runs and six wickets.

CRICKET MATCH AT HAZEL GROVE.
A cricket match was played on the Hazel Grove Cricket Ground at Norbury on Monday afternoon between Hazel Grove and Poynton. For several years past these two rival clubs have contested for supremacy, and considerable interest was taken in the match. In consequence of the annual Wakes a considerable number of people were enabled to be present and take a lively interest in the proceedings. The Hazel Grove Brass Band was in attendance and played lively selections of music during the afternoon. During the earlier part of the afternoon the rain fell in torrents, and it was thought that the match would have to be abandoned. At three o'clock, however, the time fixed for the commencement of the match, the rain cleared off, and was succeeded by brilliant sunshine. Both elevens were fairly matched up of the two clubs. Poynton, however, had a strong team, while Hazel Grove were short of the services of Gleahill, Penney, and Wood. The home captain won the toss and elected to bat. Cleaver and Fallows were the first to wield the willow, to the bowling of Rhodes and Clarke. Play was for a time rather dull, runs coming very slowly. Cleaver, the first man in, was neatly caught behind the wicket, and in breaking up Fallows' stay was very short, a solitary one falling to his lot; and Standring's career was cut short before he managed to break his duck. Roberts and Penney played well together, the latter especially batting steadily. Roberts, although he played a caution game, was only successful in obtaining four runs, Wadsworth, with a neat catch, compelling him to relinquish his bat. Only about 30 runs had been scored at four o'clock, when five wickets had fallen, and the prospect for the home eleven began to look rather gloomy. Penney, who was playing a good game, was joined by Daniels, who lost no time in breaking his duck, and by united efforts these players speedily succeeded in raising the score marked on the indicator to 40. Daniels sent a beauty to leg for two, which was speedily followed by a three. His score, too, however, now came to an end, and the next ball took his sticks. The rest of the Hazel Grove team were quickly disposed of. Smith and Clayton were the first to take their stand against the bowling of Standring and Bennett. It was soon evident to the spectators that Poynton's chances of winning were great indeed. The Poynton lads batted well, and notwithstanding the good fielding of the homesters, quickly increased the score. After a total of 53, who was the top score for Poynton was 25, made by A. Clayton. W. Bailey came second with 24 to his credit.

CHESHIRE COUNTY NEWS: FRIDAY 23 AUGUST 1895 - 2.

CRICKET.

SATURDAY'S MATCHES.
Stockport v. Werneth.
STOCKPORT WIN BRILLIANTLY.

This match between these old rivals was played at Dale Green Park in magnificent weather, and before a large crowd of spectators, it being also set apart for the benefit of the professionals, Brown and Disney, who throughout the season have done splendid work, and it is hoped that they will receive a substantial reward. It will be remembered that the first time these teams met at Werneth this season Stockport won a most interesting match by eleven runs, due on the whole to the splendid bowling of the sergeant Sam Brown. On Saturday skipper Hartley won the toss, and of course chose to bat, on a splendid wicket, taking in with him J. Bestow to face the bowling of Hall and Hodgkinson. The start was none too good from a Stockport point of view, as Bestow trying to get a full toss from Hodgkinson to leg was snappily caught at slip. Arthur Turkington joined his captain who set Hall splendidly for four, but after scoring ten he was caught at the wicket. Sam Brown came next and was loudly greeted by the crowd. He immediately got to work, scoring loose fastish bowling in rare fashion. I sustains had come when Turkington was caught by Redfern, after that player had scored six. Mickey joined his brother and batted but only to see him brilliantly caught at short slip by Collinson, after playing a splendid game. H. R. Bromley-Davenport of Cheshire county and Cambridge University now came next and here a splendid stand took place, both men defying all the efforts of the Werneth bowlers. Davenport charmed the spectators with his big hitting, while Harvey, on the other hand, was playing a most finished game, his cutting being a treat. Davenport was unfortunately run out in sprinting forward to a fast ball from Seanor, which hit the wicket keeper's pads and Seanor, which hit the wicket before Davenport could recover his ground, he had hit up 17 in a very few minutes, and he was loudly cheered on retiring. F. Tyler joined Disney, but shortly after the latter was caught at mid off, for a splendidly played innings of 21. The telegraph board now r..ading 87—6—21. F. Selby came next, but he made few further comments with the exception of Frank Tyler's display, which was a really meritorious performance. His innings ran out on the usual six fours, two three's, and three two's. He was ably assisted by J. Bestow junior, who played a tidy innings clever before being caught on the boundary. The innings closed for the respectable score of 139. After that time interval Werneth opened their venture by sending in Wharmby and Eaton, the attack being taken up in turns Brown and Bromley-Davenport. Brown opened with a maiden over, but Eaton got three, Hartley's first ball away for three, but soon after lost Wharmby, who was nicely caught by Selby at cover point, the first wicket falling at one. Hopper took Wharmby's place but with no addition to the score lost Harper twice being defeated by a grand ball from Brown. Redfern was next in and next out, Selby taking him beautifully at point off Davenport, and three wickets were down for 15 runs. Matters never altered much for with the exception of H's-north, Hall, and Seanor, no one seemed able to play the bowling, the innings closing for 30. Stockport thus place credit upon a win over Werneth for the second time this season. I must just say a few more notes of the splendid bowling Sam Brown and Harry May, the former taking five for 13, and the latter for 15 not together along with the splendid fielding of the Stockport men, who never missed a chance, was due in no small measure to their brilliant victory. The spectators seemed to fairly enjoy the afternoon's sport, and especially to see two old men come into on the right side.

MANCHESTER v. CHESHIRE HOLME.—Played on the ground of the latter. The visitors took a moderate team with them, but proved strong enough to vanquish the home lot. The game at times was very exciting, Manchester having seven wickets down and wanting 30 runs to win, but Mr. Hills (who played extremely well) on being joined by Bennett knocked off the runs. STOCKPORT CHRONICLE: MONDAY 26 AUGUST 1895-2.

SATURDAY'S MATCHES.
Stockport v. Cheadle Hulme.

Great interest was manifested in the meeting of these local rivals, which took place on the Cheadle Hulme ground in splendid weather and before a good attendance of spectators on Saturday afternoon. It was also a repeat of the benefit of the Cheadle Hulme professional, Teather. The first match between these elevens this season ended in a very even draw. Skipper Hartley lost the toss, and of course had to field. O. V. Rome and Teather were the first batsmen to open the Cheadle innings to the bowling of Sam Brown and H May. Teather reeled a single off Brown, but next over Harry May knocked his leg stump out of the ground. H Rome came next, and immediately cut Brown for four, while O Rome got May away for a like number, but was out caught by Teather taking him well at short slip. 12—2—5. Briggs joined H. Rome, but with an addition of eight runs H. Rome was finely caught by Hartley after scoring 10. A. Royle was next in, and saw Briggs nee Brown away to leg for four; and next over repeated the stroke very lovably. Royle hit May for three, but soon after that player was caught behind wicket by Harry May at short slip law down—a very fine catch indeed. H. Taylor joined Briggs, and here a stand took place, though not a very lengthy one. At 62, however, Fred Torkington, who had displaced May, then bowled Briggs, that player having made 27 in not a very taking fashion; thus half the wickets were down for 63. W. Hartley came next, but without any addition Fred Torkington upset his middle stump with one of his expresses. Taylor left at 67 after scoring 62, while Kirk left at 71, there being nine wickets down. Then came a surprise for the Stockport men. Todd and Colles on getting together made things lively for the visitors. Genuine cricket efforts were tried, but to no use, the 100 only reached amidst loud applause; both men played a fine game, Todd several times getting the ball away in nice style. W. Hartley went on with John, but created no great sensation. When the total had reached 137 Colles was bowled by Fred Torkington, his innings of 41 being at a time when things were looking serious, was of the utmost value to his side, while too much cannot be said of Todd, who carried out his bat for a splendid innings of 34. Certainly the Stockport men assisted them materially by their wretched fielding, but nevertheless they deserve great credit for their plucky partnership. Fred Torkington came out a splendid analysis out of 132 overs; he bowled six maidens for eight runs and three wickets. May had three for 25, and Brown three for 14. In ten minutes or so W. Hartley saw off J. Bates came out on behalf of Stockport, the bowling being entrusted to Teather and Redfern. Bates cut Teather finely for four, while Hartley affected Redfern soon after a similar number. Runs came at a good pace. With the score at 34 Bates was bowled by a ball from Teather which came several inches across, and removed his leg ball; that player had scored seventeen in quite. Arthur Torkington joined his captain, only to see him given out caught at the wicket, a decision which seemed doubtful. Brown came next, and here some of the finest cricket of the day was seen; both men hit out well. Still the bowling was good, but runs coming at a fair pace. Briggs displaced Teather when the score had reached 72. Torkington was bowled for a splendid innings of 24, which included three fours and four twos. Tyler came next, but after scoring 3 he was bowled. H. Hartley came next, and the first ball he received he drove it magnificently right out off the ground for four...this stroke quite taking the bowler by surprise. Sam Brown was out soon after from a big hit, which H. Rome took very well, after playing a grand game for 27, his innings included five fours and two twos. Disney came next and saw Hartley. Any about both bowlers, Briggs coming in for a fair share of punishment, he getting that player away for two fours, but in attempting to repeat was caught at the wicket, his brilliant innings of 12 included three fours, one three, one two, and a single. He tried his very utmost to bring off a win, and indeed could be said to have stayed a quarter of an hour I believe his object would have been accomplished. Disney left at the same total, 103. With May and Holby in line was called seven wickets being down for 110; thus the match ended in a draw in favour of the visitors. Below is appended full scores and analysis:—

STOCKPORT AND CHEADLE HULME 2ND.
These elevens met on Saturday afternoon at Cale Green, and a very close game resulted, owing to the smart bowling of McLaolian, who kept the visitors' score down. Hrailthwaite was the only Stockportonian who did much with the willow.

MACCLESFIELD CHRONICLE: FRIDAY 30 AUGUST 1895 - 2

Stockport v. Cheadle Hulme.

Great interest was manifested in the meeting of these local rivals, which took place on the Cheadle Hulme ground, in splendid weather, and before a good attendance of spectators on Saturday afternoon. It was also set apart as the benefit of the Cheadle Hulme professional, Teather. The first match between these elevens this season ended in a very even draw. Skipper Hartley lost the toss, and of course had to field. G. V. Brown and Teather were the first batsmen to open the Cheadle innings to the bowling of Sam Brown and H. May. Teather scored a few off Brown, but next over Harry May knocked his leg stump out of the ground. H. Rome came next, and immediately cut Brown for four, while G Home got May away for a like number, but was out soon after, Brown taking him well at short slip. 12—2—5. Briggs joined H. Rome, but with an addition of eight runs on Rome was finely caught by Hartley after scoring 10. A. Royle was next in, and saw Briggs get thrown away to leg for four, and next ball repelled the stroke very luckily. Royle hit May for three, but soon after that player was magnificently caught by Harry May at short slip low down—a very fine catch indeed. O. Taylor joined Briggs, and here a stand took place, though Briggs did most scoring. At last, however, after a fine display, Briggs had made 27.
May, clean bowled Briggs, that player having made 27 in not a very taking fashion; thus half the wickets were down for 62. W. Redfern came next, but without any addition to the score Torkington upset his middle stump with one of his expresses. Taylor left at 67 and Rome at 69, while Horn left at 71, there being nine wickets down. Then came a surprise for the Stockport men. Todd and Colles on getting together made things very lively for the fielding. Changes of bowling were tried, but to no use, the 100 going up amidst loud applause; both men played a fair game, Todd in particular batting in a brilliant Davies style. W. Hartley went on with lobs, but caused no great sensation. When the total had reached 127 Colles was bowled by Fred Torkington, his innings of 15, coming at a time when things were looking serious, was of the utmost value to his side, while too much praise cannot be paid Todd, who carried out his bat for a splendid innings of 34. Certainly the Stockport men treated their opponents with much good fielding, but nevertheless they deserve great credit for their plucky partnership. Fred Torkington came on for a spell, and in a tyst cost of 132 prove the bowl'd air maidens for eight runs and three wickets. May had three for 25, and Brown three for 35. At tea time W. Hartley, H. Hartley and J. Bates came out on behalf of Stockport, the bowling being entrusted to Teather and Redfern. Bates cut Teather away for four, while Hartley off-drove Redfern soon after for a similar number. Runs came at a good pace. With the score at 24 Bates was caught by a ball from Teather which came several inches across, and removed his leg bail; that player had scored fourteen in quick time. After Torkington joined his captain, only to see him given out caught at the wicket, a decision which seemed doubtful. Brown came next, and with some of the finer points of the game in seen, both men hit out well. Still the bowling was good, but runs coming at a fair pace. Briggs displaced Teather when the score had reached 77. Torkington was bowled for a splendid innings of 24, which included three fours and four twos. F. Tyler came next, but after scoring three was bowled. H. Hartley came next, and the first ball he received he drove it magnificently right out off Teather for four. quite taking the bowler by surprise. Sam Brown was out soon after from a big hit, which E. Rome got very well, after playing a long way on. Among his innings included five fours and two twos. Disney came next and saw Hartley lay about both bowlers, Briggs taking more than his share of punishment, he getting that player away for two fours, but in attempting to repeat was caught at the wicket, his brilliant innings of 34 included three fours, one three, one two, and a single. He tried his very utmost to bring off a win, and indeed could have stayed another over or so an hour I believe his object would have been accomplished. Disney left at the same total, 103. With May and Kirby in time and the latter being given out being down for 110 ;thus the match ended in a draw in favour of the visitors. Below is appended full scores and analysis:

STOCKPORT AND CHEADLE HULME 2ND.
These elevens met on Saturday afternoon at Cale Green, and a very close game resulted, owing to the smart bowling of McLachlan, who kept the visitors' score down. Braithwaite was the duly Stockportonian who did much with the willow.

LIVERPOOL POST: FRIDAY 13 SEPTEMBER 1895: TUESDAY 17 SEP 1895

LIVERPOOL CRICKET CLUB.

BATTING AND BOWLING AVERAGES.
The first eleven played 31 matches, won 10, lost 6, and 15 were drawn. Won: Weston, Werneth (twice), Bolton (twice), Rossall School, Boughton Hall (twice), Bootle, Warrington, Upton, Birkenhead Park, Preston, Nom. Won: New Brighton, and Oxton. Lost: Huyton, Colerne, Manchester, Formby, and Leinster (twice). Drawn: Oakmint, [twice] Hobsoken Park, Marlborough College, Clifton College, Cheltenham College, Northern, Oxton, Birkenhead Park, Fattorian -Lorrettanians, Harrow Wanderers, Washington, and Hot. Papermanuel. Runs to the number of 3,951 (including 330 extras) were scored for the loss of 311 wickets, against 5,530 runs (including 322 extras) for the loss of 342 wickets. The "an eleven" played 16 matches, won 5, lost 4, and 7 were drawn, scoring 2,282 runs (including 144 extras) for the loss of 18 wickets, against 2,603 runs (including 177 extras) for the loss of 119 wickets. The second eleven played 27 matches, won 8, lost 7, and drew 12, scoring 3,673 runs (including 311 extras) for the loss of 204 wickets, against 3,897 runs (including 302 extras) for the loss of 220 wickets. The sub eleven played 0 matches, of which 4 were won and 2 drawn. In all the club played 95 matches, of which 35 were won, 17 lost, and 50 drawn. District matches were played against Yorkshire County and Cambirdge University, the former being won and the latter lost. In addition, 3 extra matches were played, giving a grand total of 97 matches during the season. Although Mr. A. F. Kemble has only taken part in 21 matches this season, he has succeeded in stumping and catching 41 opponents.

ST. AIDAN'S.
The past season has been a most successful one for this club. Of 19 matches played the team has won 17 losing two only, and one of those by the narrow majority of 7 runs. The total number of runs they are credited with is 1,497 for 179 wickets, against 593 for 190 wickets for opponents. The highest score obtained was 133 against Brunswick Y.M. Guild. Six times during the season was the century overtopped by the Aidanites, whilst the highest score made against them was 88. G. Lewis's 70 (not out) was the highest individual score for the Saints during the season.

The First Eleven this year have done a little better than last. The averages show a big improvement.

A match between Liverpool and Oxton culminated in a win for Liverpool by 62 runs and 3 wickets. For Oxton, M. Field, H. S. Hibbert, J. Curwen were the only double figurists in a score of 71.

Rock Ferry administered a severe thrashing to Cheadle Hulme. The Ferry batted first, and after scoring 126 for 9 wickets closed their innings, and their opponents, in reply, could only muster 32. The chief scorers for Rock Ferry were J. Ravenscroft (43) and A. Stobbart (23).

New Brighton were once more obliged to knuckle under on Saturday to their conquerors this time being Formby. New Brighton, batting first, managed to amass 89 runs, chiefly through the aid of Moore (27), E. Drinkwater (11), and F. Pepper (10), these being the only New Brightonians who succeeded in reaching double figures. Formby showed to much better advantage, as they managed to compile 103 for 7 wickets.

Wallasey took on the second string of Oxton, on the latter's ground, and succeeded in defeating them by 20 runs. J. Kay (19) and G. Turner (18) being chiefly instrumental in securing Oxton's downfall.

Bootle secured an easy victory over Birkenhead Victoria, the scene of the conflict being Bootle. The Victorians batted first and scored 71, of which F. Wright compiled 22 (not out), Bootle replying with 126 for 6 wickets.

Another easy victory was that of Bromboro' over Spital, whom they swamped to the tune of 61 with 4 wickets to spare. For Bromboro' the chief scorers were found in J. Pugh with 50, and H. Pugh with 36, while for the losers W. Bowring and G. Earl were first with 22 and 11 respectively.

Tranmere Wesley overcame West Derby 2nd by sixteen runs, J. Turnbull (12) being the only double figurist in the match. Buckley and Quinn in the bowling department took 4 wickets each at a cost of thirteen runs.

Y.M.C.A. finished a generally successful season by defeating Ravenscroft by the substantial majority of 61, E. R. Davies, R. Willacev, and L. Bunting showing good form with the bat for scores of 26, 12, and 11 respectively.

BIRKENHEAD NEWS: SATURDAY 14 SEPTEMBER 1895 - 2.

CRICKET NOTES.

Saturday saw the practical conclusion of the season, the leading local clubs all finishing their list of engagements. The Premier club should have played Huyton, but as the latter's ground was nothing short of a quagmire after the heavy rain of the previous evening, the match had perforce to be abandoned. It is some time back now since the Parkites have had such a successful season as the one just concluded, as their position at the head of the districts competition readily testifies. Independent, however, of their excellent record against the district clubs, they have done more than well against such powerful opponents as those of Manchester, Leyland and Wigan, the latter being beaten in both their engagements with the Park club. It will be seen on reference to the batting and bowling averages that T. R. Hubbeck heads the list in both departments of the game, a position which indicates what an invaluable acquisition he has been to his club with both bat and ball, independent of the great service he has rendered behind the wicket. J. Findling Ould has secured the second position in the batting list, being closely followed by H. J. Fish, who, owing to a severe illness has been prevented from taking part in several important matches. The successful skipper Holden can hardly be said to have played up to the form exhibited by him for several previous years, and it looks a trifle curious to see his name so low down in the list as fourth, but still an average of 31·11 for 26 innings is by no means bad, and of course this he has done excellent service with the ball, having captured 45 wickets at an average cost of 9·20. Indeed he has seldom bowled better than he has done this season, and he is to be congratulated on his capital record with the sphere. H. M. Grayson comes out fairly well with an average of 19·1 for 16 innings, but Smith shows a great falling off as compared with last year, his figure being 16·3 for 19 ventures. Town has done a little better, he having an average of 16 for 25 innings, whilst others who figure rather low down, but who may be confidently expected to do much better in the future, include H. W. P. Jannette, H. Salmon, and H. C. Cochrane. That good old stonewaller, A. B. Wilson, does not appear to have exercised his usual discretion, for he comes very near to being the "absolute," this unenviable position being occupied by Captain Byrne. The brunt of the bowling has of course being borne by Smith, who has taken 53 wickets for 10·9, whilst C. E. Steen's 48 have been secured at a rate of 13·7. Town has had a singularly unfortunate season, although he has bowled uniformly well he has been able to get but few wickets, 34 at a cost of 22·11 being rather expensive.
   The Rock Ferryites concluded a fairly successful season on Saturday with a win over Cheadle Hulme. Of the 25 matches they have played, 11 have been won, 6 drawn, and 7 lost, whilst one had the almost unique result of a tie. A glance at the batting averages shows E. F. Kearsey at the head of affairs with the nice figures of 30·88 for nine innings, and it seems rather a pity that his services are not more often available for first team matches. A. J. Cripps comes next, but his average compares unfavourably with that of Kearsey, there being a considerable difference between 30·88 and 23, albeit Cripps has played two more innings. With the exception of his captain, A. Stott, who is placed third, has taken part in more matches than any other player in the team, and his 21·13 for 24 innings must be set down as distinctly creditable. G. G. Paton has an average of 20·4 for 14 innings, whilst immediately following him comes "Capting" Ravenscroft who, on the whole, has been far from fortunate, repeated failures reducing his figures to as low as 19·79 for 26 innings. Another batsman who has not shown to great advantage this season is T. R. Brotherton, whose figures of 19·66 for 29 attempts are not as good as might be expected from such a capable willow wielder, whilst the average of A. C. Blain is also a little disappointing, this usually remarkably vigorous batsman being comparatively low down in the list with 19·33 for 18 innings. Needham's figures are 17·28 for 23 attempts, the next in order of merit being A. C. Bamford, who for 16 innings has an average of 14·46. Surprisingly low down is J. S. Bamford who, however, has not devoted much time to the crease, having only been at the wickets on six occasions, for which he has an average of 10·14. J. Bretherton, E. Stott, G. B. Paterson, and E. J. Ryland have also filled places in the list, the last being Ryland who, out of 14 innings, has been not out no less than seven times, and would certainly have had a much higher average than 4·14 if he had been given a chance of showing his abilities with the bat. If he has not proved himself a brilliant batsman, however, there can be no question about his success with the ball, for during the season he has captured no fewer than 113 wickets at the moderate rate of 11·03 per wicket. J. Bretherton, though bowling well, falls far behind Ryland, the fast bowler only crediting himself with 35 wickets at a cost of 12·36. With such strong amateur bowling talent at its disposal, the club was not required to call upon the services of Needham to any great extent, but the pro has been very useful at times, and has secured 26 wickets at an average cost of 17·19.
   Though the Oxtonites have been under a cloud for the last two or three weeks, they cannot be said to have fared badly on the whole, as out of 26 matches played they have won 9 and drawn 13, being absolutely beaten on but five occasions, one the match referred to in my remarks about Rock Ferry, resulting in a tie. On Saturday, at Aigburth, they met with another serious reverse, receiving a shocking trouncing at the hands of the Liverpool representatives, who disposed of them for 71, and knocked up 133 for the loss of seven wickets. The Oxtonites thus ended the season with three successive losses. Their batting averages reveal the fact that M. Court has not only scored the most runs but he has also the best average, his figures being 32·67 for 27 innings, a really excellent record for this very promising young player. The second position on the list is filled by J. H. F. Grayson, with 27·67 for nine innings, but now that this undoubtedly fine batsman has definitely thrown in his lot with the Oxtonites, we may expect to see a marked improvement in his figures next year. Another ex-Park player takes third being G. F. Court. J. V. Bishop has developed into one of the mainstays of the Oxton batting, this being evident by his excellent average of 25·67 for 25 innings. The Oxton skipper, C. F. Hutton has been a little off colour occasionally during the season, and has not scored quite so prolifically as he has done in former years, his highest contribution in an innings being 52, and his average 20·38 for 15 ventures. That the new pro. Bishop will be a great acquisition to the Oxtonites next season there can be but little doubt, for during the short time he has been engaged he has done wonderfully well with both bat and ball, having a batting average of 37·20 for 5 innings, whilst with the ball he has secured 43 wickets at a cost of 9·4 per wicket. J. Curwen has scored better and more consistently than any other for a considerable time, and his record of 19·12 for 20 innings indicates that his powers as a batsman have not yet altogether left him. H. Chambers has only taken part in 6 innings for which his figures are 16·17, whilst for 10 innings M. Field has an average of 14·22. Through an enforced absence early on in the season, Smith was unable to take as active a part in the campaign as could be wished, and for his 12 innings he is rather low down on the list with 13·52. G. Bickerstaffe has played in ten matches, and has scarcely been so successful in taking out his bat as he has been in former seasons, consequently his average has suffered somewhat, and his figures of 11·20 are not calculated to make him unduly conceited. G. H. Court, B. S. Smith, and P. L. Bromnell fill in close-together figures, the ranging from 10·33 to 8·18, L. Court bringing up the rear with 3·36 for 2 innings. Bowling honours are divided between amateurs and professionals, Bishop coming out well with 43 wickets at a cost of 9·4. Smith has proved a trifle more expensive his figures being 63 for 9·62, but his record is an excellent one in every particular, especially in view of the accident he met with, before referred to. G. H. Court has also rendered splendid service with the ball, capturing no fewer than 48 wickets, whilst his younger brother L. Court has given signs of future usefulness by securing 12 wickets for 3·36 per wicket.
   Like that of Oxton, the Birkenhead Victoria first string have been faring badly of late, and also like Oxton they concluded their campaign on Saturday with a disastrous defeat, the Bootle representatives, who have done anything but well themselves this year, achieving an easy victory over the unfortunate Birkenhead team side who made a very feeble show with the bat, and were all sent to the rightabout for 71. On the whole the Victoria representatives can hardly be congratulated on their season's record, for out of 25 matches they have only won four, whilst 9 have been lost and 12 drawn. It is not surprising to see J. Wylde at the head of the batting averages, as he has been the most consistent good form throughout the season. Others who may be said to have done well are only T. Davies (28·8 for 12 innings and 149·8?), J. Routledge (18·7) and J. Macdonald (17·3), but a falling off is noticeable in the batting of J. Brocklebank, who is very low down on the list with 14·6, though he has played in more matches than any of his colleagues. J. Fish has been a distinct acquisition with the feather and heads the bowling averages with 57 wickets and a little over 11 runs per wicket. So far as taking wickets is concerned, however, J. Brocklebank is an easy first, he having captured 42 at a cost of 14·22. Several other players have also had a trial with the ball, these including J. West, S. Wright, M. Sprat, J. Wylde, E. H. Carter, and W. H. Routledge.
